OPEC+ Production Policy\nIn early January 2026, OPEC+ announced the suspension of its scheduled production increases for Q1 2026, reflecting clear concerns about oversupply and ongoing sanctions on major producers such as Russia. This pause is meant to stabilize Brent prices, following recent inventory builds despite existing disruptions ([AP News](https://apnews.com/article/790431afcabf60aad64075c4979ab606?utm_source=openai), Jan 2026).\n\n## 2. Price Movements and Supply Outlook\nBrent crude prices continued a notable downward trend, with the December 2025 average falling to $63 per barrel\u2014an $11 YoY decrease. This decline is chiefly attributed to persistent production growth (even after reductions), coupled with expanding inventories, which have reached four-year highs. Overall sentiment is bearish, with projections for 2026\u20132027 suggesting further pressure: the EIA and industry analysts see Brent testing the $56\u201362 range across 2026 ([IEA Oil Market Report, Dec 2025](https://www.iea.org/reports/oil-market-report-december-2025?utm_source=openai); [Tradingnews.com](https://www.tradingnews.com/news/oil-price-forecast-can-brent-hold-60-usd?utm_source=openai)).\n\n## 3. Analyst Forecasts and Market Sentiment\nA new Reuters economist poll and revisions by major banks (JPMorgan, UBS) show a clear downward adjustment in Brent forecasts, reflecting mounting fears of a global surplus and subdued demand. Consensus estimates expect Brent to average $62.23 for 2026, with further risk of slippage. Market participants are discounting concerns related to past geopolitical risks, given the supply overhang ([Reuters cited in Tradingnews.com](https://www.tradingnews.com/news/oil-price-forecast-can-brent-hold-60-usd?utm_source=openai)).\n\n## 4. Global Inventories and Demand/Supply\nWhile OPEC+ production cuts have brought some supply cuts\u2014610,000 bpd drop in November 2025\u2014global inventories surged to four-year highs in October. This disconnect signals that, despite headline production cuts from OPEC+ (especially Russia and Venezuela), demand growth is not keeping pace, intensifying the bearish tilt in the Brent market ([IEA, Dec 2025](https://www.iea.org/reports/oil-market-report-december-2025?utm_source=openai)).\n\n## 5. The Debate in a Nutshell \nBull\u2019s strongest cards \n\u2022 Rate-of-change: U.S. imports are finally falling and a first weekly draw is showing up. \n\u2022 Technical confirmation: price has reclaimed the 50- and 200-day averages with momentum still building, giving CTAs a green light. \n\u2022 OPEC+ pause plus Red-Sea risk keeps the market in backwardation, providing a positive roll yield and a geopolitical \u201cfloor.\u201d \n\nBear\u2019s strongest cards \n\u2022 Inventories are still at 4-year highs; every agency forecast for 2026 shows a surplus and $56\u201362 Brent. \n\u2022 OPEC+ is acting defensively after the fact; prior \u201ccuts\u201d have not stopped the build. \n\u2022 The recent rally is event-driven (Suez/Red Sea) and has already started to fade as freight rates normalize. \n\u2022 Structural drift: Brent\u2019s long-dated liquidity and benchmark dominance are slipping versus WTI/Oman\u2014making upside follow-through harder. \n\u2022 History rhymes: 2018, 2019 and 2022 all produced identical \u201ctechnical breakouts\u201d that failed when the physical oversupply re-asserted itself.\n\nThe single most compelling evidence on each side \n\u2022 Bull: persistent backwardation despite bearish narrative\u2014rare unless prompt barrels are genuinely wanted. \n\u2022 Bear: the hard inventory data\u2014four-year-high stocks and every major body still projecting surplus through 2026.\n\n2. My Decision \u2013 SELL (align with the Bear) \nWhy? \nThe inventory glut is real, documented, and has endured through several OPEC+ \u201crescues.\u201d Until multiple consecutive draws appear, every historical analog says rallies sputter. The bull case rests too heavily on one weekly import dip, technicals, and geopolitical roulette. In commodities, stocks rule; price action follows fundamentals with a lag, not vice-versa.\n\n3. Investment Plan \n\nA. Core Structural RISKS \u2014 Inventory, Oversupply, and Fundamental Weakness Trump Short-Term \u201cTightening\u201d\n\n**Bull Claim:** \u201cInventory builds are \u2018stale\u2019 news. Market cares about marginal change; OPEC+ is acting early; price basing signals a regime shift.\u201d\n\n**Reality Check:**\n\n- **Inventory Headwinds Remain Overwhelming.** \n The core driver of the 2026 outlook is persistent oversupply. As recently as December, *global crude inventories stood at four-year highs* (IEA, Dec 2025). Even after recent U.S. import declines, the *stockpile glut is not resolved\u2014it's entrenched*. No sustainable oil bull market in history has launched from this position; the market simply cannot ignore that reality.\n\n - **Lesson from Past Cycles:** In 2018, 2019, and late 2022, oil bulls also bet on \u201crate of change\u201d arguments at supply peaks\u2014only to get whipsawed as persistent high stockpiles eventually forced prices and curves lower. The risk is betting on a single weekly draw while the supertanker-sized \u201cglut\u201d looms above all.\n\n- **OPEC+ Policy\u2014Defending the Lows, Not Launching the Rally.** \n The \u201cpause\u201d on Q1 2026 increases is a *reactive* flinch, not preemptive tightening: **OPEC+ cut only after inventories ballooned and prices dropped double-digits YoY**. This is the behaviour of a group that is losing its grip\u2014not one forecasting upside. The group\u2019s repeated failure to stem builds, despite cut promises, directly undermines bullish confidence.\n\n- **Price Action is Not a Regime Shift\u2014It\u2019s a Bounce after Panic Selling.** \n The reclaim of averages and a mini-rally is highly suspect when it coincides with one-off event spikes (VLCC surges, Suez scare). Remember: *dead cat bounces* are a hallmark of late-cycle commodity markets. If these levels hold, why do every major agency and sell-side analyst see $56\u2013$62 as the range ceiling? Momentum traders routinely get trapped in whipsaws driven by volatile event headlines. Current ATR and volatility readings actually warn that meaningful trend extension *requires* new, persistent real-world supply-demand tightening\u2014not just price noise.\n\n - **Lesson Learned:** In earlier cycles, I too read too much into \u201cconfluence\u201d without respect for macro supply overhangs. As soon as VLCC rates retreated (-42% in a week after panic), spreads and risk premia collapsed. This is \u201crented\u201d backwardation, not earned through demand tightening.\n\n---\n\n# III. Brent Benchmark Weakness and Liquidity Erosion: Strategic Vulnerability Exposed\n\n**Bull Claim:** \"Brent remains the premier global benchmark, deeply liquid and widely used.\"\n\n**Reality Check:**\n\n- **Market Share is Shrinking.** \n Growth is coming from WTI and new Asian benchmarks. Brent is increasingly tethered to a shrinking base of North Sea output, forcing Basket methodology adjustments to paper over declining volumes. This risks pricing anomalies, discourages global macro and systematic flows, and erodes Brent\u2019s network effects.\n\n - *Even major Asian refiners are now referencing Oman and Shanghai benchmarks for key deals\u2014a dilution of Brent\u2019s iron grip on global trade.*\n\n- **Liquidity In Long-Dated Contracts Is Abysmal.** \n Deferred Brent futures show declining open interest and thinner spreads. Programmatic/CTA adoption lags WTI, hampering the efficient implementation of systematic trend or mean-reversion models. This isn\u2019t academic: thinning liquidity *magnifies volatility, widens spreads, and raises the risk of price dislocations*.\n\n - **Lesson:** In the late 2010s, as WTI microstructure improved, money flowed away from Brent in hotly traded contracts. Fundamentals *moved markets*, not merely \u201clegacy benchmark\u201d status.\n\n---\n\n# IV. The risk here is being caught in precisely the kind of \u201cevent spike\u201d you claim to exploit\u2014only, as the seller, you\u2019re on the *wrong* side if sentiment runs further or headlines unexpectedly worsen. Given the current modest volatility, there\u2019s a much greater risk that stops are run *on the short side* during a low-liquidity gap, causing not just simple drawdown but potentially multi-standard deviation moves against you before trailing stops can even be hit.\n\nLet\u2019s also examine your \u201cstructural\u201d trade arguments\u2014calendar spreads, backwardation, etc. You\u2019re correct that short-term logistics panic has propped up backwardation, but you neglect to factor in that backwardated curves in oil don\u2019t always normalize instantly, especially when physical disruptions and speculative flows persist. The recent drop in VLCC freight rates has *not* erased all transport concerns, as GPRD_THREAT indices and the ongoing options volatility indicate. If we do see renewed shipping panic or supply chain issues\u2014even minor ones\u2014another backwardation spike could savage short calendar spread positions. Structuring a short that relies on \u201ccurve normalization\u201d under these macro risks is reckless. This isn\u2019t a 2018-style steady unwind. The tools that may have \u201cworked\u201d in past mean reversion cycles can and will fail in the face of today\u2019s more complex, multi-polar risk structure.\n\nYour favorite refrain is that \u201cinaction\u201d or \u201chedged neutrality\u201d cedes alpha to others. But in reality, *preservation of capital* and *prevention of catastrophic loss* is how you protect alpha over the cycle\u2014and how you avoid dramatic multi-month recoveries (if not outright permanent drawdowns) after just one missed risk event. With inventories at four-year highs, global agencies projecting continued oversupply, and every major bank revising Brent targets *down* towards the mid- to low-$60s in 2026, the real opportunity here is for steady, disciplined risk-taking\u2014not for running after every short-lived mispricing. That means resisting the urge to \u201cbet big\u201d right as technical signals attract the most systematic buying and options volatility sharply inflates hedging costs.\n\nMoreover, your approach massively underestimates the liquidity, slippage, and tail risk associated with shorting a structurally volatile asset in a regime dominated by rapid event reversals. Every one of your \u201chistoric analogs\u201d also included periods where counter-trend moves\u2014particularly in crowded short setups\u2014led to painful, forced covering and negative convexity. Simply put, what worked in 2018 or 2022 is not a guarantee in 2026, especially with macro uncertainty, rising AI-driven headline trading, and higher baseline geopolitical risk premiums.\n\nTo sum up: The genuinely prudent course is to *reduce risk exposure* at trend inflection points such as this, not to ramp up short risk under cover of \u201crobust overlays.\u201d The real value to the firm is in *avoiding whipsaw and unrewarded volatility*; in today\u2019s market, that means sizing down, favoring more delta-neutral, inventory-anchored pairs, or dialing back outright directional bets until confirmation from *multiple* weekly draws or a confirmed reversion in both technicals and sentiment. Asset protection\u2014not mere alpha chasing\u2014wins the long game.\n\nSo before acting, ask yourself: is the firm here to survive and steadily grow, or is it out to gamble on timing every fade and headline? If capital preservation and sustainable profits are the mandate, your aggressive short is simply unjustifiable in its current form.", "neutral_history": "\nNeutral Analyst: Let\u2019s step in between these two poles and have a frank discussion about what each of you is missing\u2014and how a neutral, adaptive framework can capture opportunity without leaving the portfolio exposed to regime-change \u201cblind spots.\u201d\n\nTo the Risky Analyst: \nYour hunger for seizing volatility and rapid technical reversals is exactly the kind of conviction that can generate strong returns\u2014when matched with the right macro context. But you\u2019re leaning far too hard on the idea that all bullish moves are simply \u201cevent risk froth\u201d and that the breakout is just waiting to fade. Here\u2019s where that reads as both a strength and a risk:\n\nYou\u2019re absolutely correct that this market\u2019s rallies have, historically, fizzled out amid persistent supply. The case for fading overbought spikes is legitimate\u2014**IF** supply and inventories begin to matter again in the narrative. But the problem right now is that for the first time in months, we have *all classic technicals*\u2014the 10-, 50-, and 200-day averages, MACD, RSI\u2014turning bullish in sync, at a major support zone, with momentum that is confirmed but not yet stretched. That\u2019s not just \u201cfroth\u201d\u2014that\u2019s the exact setup where systematic, quant, and passive flows start to buy dips instead of sell rallies.\n\nYou say we should sell aggressively on the back of premature optimism, driven by event headlines. But if you act too early\u2014without further confirmation from actual cracks in price action\u2014there\u2019s a real risk you\u2019ll be the stepping stone for the next wave of systematic buyers. Your own \u201cevent-driven\u201d thesis cuts both ways: what if (as the safe analyst notes), another headline (tanker attack, supply hiccup, or even just a persistent lack of inventory builds) appears? If this is the beginning of a regime shift, not a temporary pop, you\u2019re essentially standing in front of a freight train while volatility is still expanding. Yes\u2014event-driven spikes present opportunity\u2014but waiting for failed breakouts or confirmed reversals gives you better odds than full conviction shorts into what might be only the first leg of a bull reversal.\n\nTo the Safe Analyst: \nYou make a strong case for capital preservation, and yes, ignoring the reality of high inventories and cautious long-term forecasts is shortsighted. However, your argument tips into excessive caution by claiming now is exactly when to size *down* or avoid outright directionality. Here\u2019s the problem with that stance:\n\nThe data do not support \u201csit on your hands.\u201d Social sentiment and technicals are both flashing early-stage bull, but **not** outright euphoria, and volatility (while elevated last week) remains relatively subdued compared to past event-driven regimes. Your insistence that downside risks must always be the default ignores the possibility that a \u201cbullish regime shift\u201d\u2014even if only temporary\u2014is exactly when underexposed portfolios get left behind. The market is *not* brimming with crowded long positions; in fact, systematic money is only now starting to engage above the 200-day average for the first time in months. Waiting for multiple weeks of inventory draws or a \u201cquiet\u201d confirmation could easily see Brent at $70+ before slower money gets involved. At that point, the risk/reward for new shorts is actually much worse.\n\nAlso, while you\u2019re correct that options hedging has become expensive, you overlook the potential benefits of *selectively* monetizing elevated implied volatility\u2014there are ways to structure options spreads or collars that protect against event spikes without bleeding premium in a sideways grind.\n\nWhere Both Arguments Fall Short\u2014and What a Balanced Path Looks Like: \nNeither \u201caggressive short here\u201d nor \u201ctotal risk-off\u201d is optimal. There\u2019s a time to size up and a time to reduce exposure, but the present signal is mixed: short-term and medium-term price action has flipped bullish, social sentiment has revived, and inventory and long-term supply/demand suggest any strength will eventually be capped.\n\nThe moderate, **sustainable** play is to:\n\n- **Size down the outright short.** If you want to express the bearish supply case, do it with partial exposure\u2014don\u2019t go full conviction until (a) price loses the 10- and 50-day averages, and/or (b) the next weekly inventory data confirms a resumption of builds or a failed draw. \n- **Use option hedges, but favor defined-risk structures.** Protect against near-term spikes by using tight, cost-effective puts to limit mark-to-market risk instead of \u201copen-ended\u201d short deltas. Option spreads/collars involving both calls and puts keep hedging costs manageable while protecting exposure. \n- **Explore calendar or pairs trades with less outright directionality.** A short calendar spread or a pairs trade versus a more supply-constrained product (e.g., jet fuel or products with bullish physical setups) enables you to stay positioned for curve normalization and structural weakness if supply reasserts itself, while reducing outright directional pain. \n- **Let trend-following signals guide reversals.** If price closes below the 62.50\u201363 level on a daily basis and MACD/RSI momentum turns down, scale into your short. If price holds the 10- and 50-day averages and momentum improves, reduce bearish bias and look for more neutral/long-biased set-ups. \n- **Keep liquidity and event monitoring at the front of your process.** With GPRD_THREAT and OVX bouncing all over, position-sizing discipline and speed of response are critical\u2014you must be ready to either cut risk or flip with fresh news. No set-and-forget.\n\n**In summary:** \nThe best approach blends the Risky Analyst\u2019s tactical opportunism **with** the Safe Analyst\u2019s appreciation for regime risks and capital protection. Take a starter short, but with moderate size and robust, *cost-effective* options protection. Be ready to add if the macro/fundamental picture turns further bearish and technicals confirm. But equally, don\u2019t ignore fresh uptrends\u2014if price holds and squeezes higher on further risk, be nimble and cut back.\n\nDon\u2019t just fade price or hide in your shell: stay active, keep risk scalable, and pivot as confirmation or invalidation emerges. That\u2019s the only way to manage both upside and downside in a regime with both bear-surplus fundamentals\u2014and newly-awakened technical and headline momentum." } } }

OPEC+ Production Policy\nIn early January 2026, OPEC+ announced the suspension of its scheduled production increases for Q1 2026, reflecting clear concerns about oversupply and ongoing sanctions on major producers such as Russia. This pause is meant to stabilize Brent prices, following recent inventory builds despite existing disruptions ([AP News](https://apnews.com/article/790431afcabf60aad64075c4979ab606?utm_source=openai), Jan 2026).\n\n## 2. Price Movements and Supply Outlook\nBrent crude prices continued a notable downward trend, with the December 2025 average falling to $63 per barrel\u2014an $11 YoY decrease. This decline is chiefly attributed to persistent production growth (even after reductions), coupled with expanding inventories, which have reached four-year highs. Overall sentiment is bearish, with projections for 2026\u20132027 suggesting further pressure: the EIA and industry analysts see Brent testing the $56\u201362 range across 2026 ([IEA Oil Market Report, Dec 2025](https://www.iea.org/reports/oil-market-report-december-2025?utm_source=openai); [Tradingnews.com](https://www.tradingnews.com/news/oil-price-forecast-can-brent-hold-60-usd?utm_source=openai)).\n\n## 3. Analyst Forecasts and Market Sentiment\nA new Reuters economist poll and revisions by major banks (JPMorgan, UBS) show a clear downward adjustment in Brent forecasts, reflecting mounting fears of a global surplus and subdued demand. Consensus estimates expect Brent to average $62.23 for 2026, with further risk of slippage. Market participants are discounting concerns related to past geopolitical risks, given the supply overhang ([Reuters cited in Tradingnews.com](https://www.tradingnews.com/news/oil-price-forecast-can-brent-hold-60-usd?utm_source=openai)).\n\n## 4. Global Inventories and Demand/Supply\nWhile OPEC+ production cuts have brought some supply cuts\u2014610,000 bpd drop in November 2025\u2014global inventories surged to four-year highs in October. This disconnect signals that, despite headline production cuts from OPEC+ (especially Russia and Venezuela), demand growth is not keeping pace, intensifying the bearish tilt in the Brent market ([IEA, Dec 2025](https://www.iea.org/reports/oil-market-report-december-2025?utm_source=openai)).\n\n## 5. Geopolitical Considerations\nGeopolitical risk premiums have moderated since the peak of Iran\u2019s threats to close the Strait of Hormuz (mid-2025), which fueled brief price spikes and market nervousness. The risk remains in the background, but its effect has diminished as supply-side surpluses and soft demand currently dominate the narrative ([Wikipedia \u2013 Iran Threat, Jun 2025](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2025_Iran_threat_of_Strait_of_Hormuz_closure?utm_source=openai)).\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Date | Event | Net Impact (%) | Rationale | Source & URL |\n|--------------|-----------------------------------------------|----------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------|\n| 2025-12-01 | Global inventories rise to 4-year highs | -45% | Oversupply indications/reduced upward price pressure despite OPEC+ cuts | IEA, https://www.iea.org/reports/oil-market-report-december-2025?utm_source=openai |\n| 2025-12-24 | Brent crude falls to $63 avg. in Dec 2025 | -55% | Persistent supply growth and price outlook negative; Let\u2019s look at the foundation:\n\n- **Inventory Builds Matter.** Historically, inventory overhangs are a powerful drag on spot and future curves, forcing repeated resets lower. The December 2025 Brent price ($63) is **down $11 YoY** (a 15%+ decline) for exactly this reason.\n- **OPEC+ Policy Is Defensive, Not Proactive.** The most recent production pause is a sign of scrambling for balance\u2014not strength. Pauses haven\u2019t prevented further build-ups. Recent bullish spikes are *reactionary* to geopolitical events, not a return to healthy demand.\n- **Sell-Side Projections Are Still Falling:** As of January 2026, consensus estimates for Brent are **$56\u2013$62** for 2026\u2014*below* today\u2019s prompt price ([Reuters/Tradingnews.com](https://www.tradingnews.com/news/oil-price-forecast-can-brent-hold-60-usd?utm_source=openai)). The path of least resistance remains DOWN.\n\n---\n\n### 2. Technical and Sentiment Analysis: The \u201cBreakout\u201d is a False Dawn\n\n- **Short-Term Rally \u2260 Structural Upturn.** The bulls hang their argument on the recent reclaim of 200-day and 50-day averages, but this coincided with the sharpest VLCC rate spike and \u201cevent-driven\u201d price rally in months\u2014directly attributable to Red Sea/Suez disruptions. These supply shocks are ephemeral, not sustainable trend catalysts.\n- **Backwardation Is Not Proof of Underlying Strength:** The prompt-forward curve may be in backwardation because of *logistical panic*\u2014not real supply shortage. Once shipping lanes normalize, these differentials evaporate, and we return to roll-losses for long-holders if the flat price resumes its decline.\n- **Social Sentiment Is Flimsy:** Past cycles demonstrate: bullish crowding (-20 to +50% swings in sentiment in December-January alone) is highly sensitive to headlines but unwinds just as fast when the reality of inventories, weak refining margins, and demand shortfalls return to the fore.\n\n---\n\n### 3. Competitive and Liquidity Vulnerabilities\n\n- **Brent\u2019s Market Share Erosion:** Contrary to the myth of irrepressible liquidity, recent data shows deferred Brent (long-dated futures) liquidity thinning, with open interest and bid/offer depth waning relative to WTI and DME Oman. This reflects the growing irrelevance of North Sea production, as new U.S., Middle Eastern, and Asian grades take share in both physical and financial markets. \n \u2013 **Strategic Risk:** As alternative benchmarks rise, Brent-linked trading becomes more vulnerable to shocks, less attractive to algorithmic and systematic traders who require robust depth in all maturities.\n- **Innovation Gap:** WTI has leapfrogged Brent in electronic trading model adoption and microstructure upgrades, making trend/momentum systems less sticky in Brent. This limits the upside (and risk-managed downside) participation of global macro players\u2014reducing the \u201cfollow-through\u201d odds for any breakout.\n\n---\n\n### 4. Adverse Market Indicators\n\n- **Forward Curves and Positioning:** \n \u2013 *Any* recent backwardation is minor and volatile. Past weeks saw sharp swings between flat, shallow backwardation, and contango (prompt premiums vanish with each passing shipping update). \n \u2013 **Inventories at Four-Year Highs:** No bullish cycle in history was built from multi-year supply gluts. \n \u2013 **Volatility Risks Are Blurring, Not Confirming, Upside:** ATR is low, but .OVX spiked +30% in January, and volatility is expanding again on risk-off news, not healthy spot market tightness.\n- **Macro/Geopolitical Headwinds:** \n \u2013 The market absorbed mid-January\u2019s elevated \u201cthreat\u201d levels almost exclusively through a \u201crenting of premium\u201d\u2014a short squeeze, not real conviction. \n \u2013 With every \u201cheadline\u201d fade (January 19\u201323: VLCC rates plunge back down -41.6%; Suez panic abating), risk premium melts and prices stall.\n\n---\n\n### 5. Countering the Bull\u2019s Structural Argument\u2014Point by Point\n\n**A. \u201cBrent is the Benchmark\u2014Liquidity, Physical Link, and Roll Yields Will Persist\u201d** \n\u2013 Brent\u2019s benchmark supremacy is no longer absolute (shrinking North Sea output and lingering Dated Brent pricing disputes undermine trust). \n\u2013 Increasing competition from WTI, and crude delivered to Europe from the U.S. Gulf Coast (notably since 2022), means Brent can lose market share\u2014hurting the network effects for futures and spreads.\n\n**B. \u201cBackwardation, Technical Momentum, and Positioning Confirm the Upturn\u201d** \n\u2013 These are *short-lived*, event-driven features, constantly reversed as inventory and macro weakness reassert. The bear side of the curve will re-appear as physical sellers rush in above $66 (well within the recent range), and the trend will fail if the 10/50/200-day averages are breached, as occurred twice in 2025\u2019s failed rallies.\n\n**C. \u201cOPEC+ Will Always Rescue the Market\u201d** \n\u2013 This \u201cOPEC put\u201d is losing credibility: Actual production cuts have so far failed to meaningfully dent inventories. Every time discipline is \u201cproven,\u201d it\u2019s in response to crisis, not as preemption\u2014an unreliable safety net at best.\n\n**D. \u201cGeopolitical Risk Means Asymmetrical Upside\u201d** \n\u2013 Recent price rallies are solely high-volatility trades on \u201cwar premium.\u201d As soon as tankers reroute, or shipping risk abates, these gains collapse\u2014leaving long-only investors exposed to renewed grind lower.\n\n---\n\n## II. Lessons from Past Cycles: Don\u2019t Get Sucked into Bull Traps\n\n**Reflections and Improvements:** \n- In past cycles (e.g., 2021 and 2019), I over-indexed on \u201ctechnical reclaim\u201d and threw caution to the wind on base-building breakouts. The result: profitless whipsaws each time supply, inventories, and demand headwinds overpowered fleeting price momentum.\n- *Key improvement:* The real \u201cfat pitch\u201d for oil bulls only comes when supply/demand has turned and inventories are being liquidated week on week\u2014not flat, not building, and not simply \u201cless bad.\u201d\n- This is not that setup. Every bullish argument today is predicated on avoidance of headline risk, not the core trend in physical balances.\n\n---\n\n## III. Trade Structure and Risk\n\n- **ATR stops are tight today because realized volatility is low\u2014but with .OVX up +10% this week and macro headline risk everywhere, stop-outs and slippage risk have risen.*\n- **Downside Catalysts:** A close back under $62.50 (below all key moving averages) is not far off\u2014one soft U.S. or Asian PMI print, or the rapid re-resolution of current Red Sea shipping disruption, could send Brent 5% lower in a matter of days.\n\n---\n\n## IV. Conclusion: Why the Bear Case Still Dominates\n\n- **Persistent oversupply, multi-year inventory gluts, and waning competitive advantages leave little justification for structural long positions in Brent.**\n- **Technical and sentiment-driven rallies are thin, driven by fleeting geopolitical worries, not durable macro shifts.**\n- **Liquidity and innovation gaps hurt Brent\u2019s attractiveness versus WTI and new regional benchmarks.**\n- **The \u201cOPEC put\u201d is reactive, not preventive\u2014offering unreliable support at best.**\n- **The best risk/reward today is to fade rallies and position for mean reversion down to the $56\u201362 range forecast by both agency and bank consensus.**\n\n**Unless you have unique edge in capturing fleeting event-driven breakouts or deploying short-dated options, investing behind the Brent rally is a case of \u201cpicking up nickels in front of a steamroller.\u201d The real smart money in oil knows: When the fundamentals and positioning say \u2018risk-off,\u2019 there\u2019s no shame in sitting out\u2014or getting short.**\n\n---\n\n**Bear Case Stance:** \nSell Brent rallies, hedge with puts, and do not chase event-driven \u201cbreakouts.\u201d The downside is real, the higher highs are ephemeral, and the odds favor a grind lower as oversupply and tepid demand reassert control. As recently as December, *global crude inventories stood at four-year highs* (IEA, Dec 2025). Even after recent U.S. import declines, the *stockpile glut is not resolved\u2014it's entrenched*. This is the behaviour of a group that is losing its grip\u2014not one forecasting upside. The group\u2019s repeated failure to stem builds, despite cut promises, directly undermines bullish confidence.\n\n- **Price Action is Not a Regime Shift\u2014It\u2019s a Bounce after Panic Selling.** \n The reclaim of averages and a mini-rally is highly suspect when it coincides with one-off event spikes (VLCC surges, Suez scare). Momentum traders routinely get trapped in whipsaws driven by volatile event headlines. Current ATR and volatility readings actually warn that meaningful trend extension *requires* new, persistent real-world supply-demand tightening\u2014not just price noise.\n\n - **Lesson Learned:** In earlier cycles, I too read too much into \u201cconfluence\u201d without respect for macro supply overhangs. As soon as VLCC rates retreated (-42% in a week after panic), spreads and risk premia collapsed. This is \u201crented\u201d backwardation, not earned through demand tightening.\n\n---\n\n# III. Brent Benchmark Weakness and Liquidity Erosion: Strategic Vulnerability Exposed\n\n**Bull Claim:** \"Brent remains the premier global benchmark, deeply liquid and widely used.\"\n\n**Reality Check:**\n\n- **Market Share is Shrinking.** \n Growth is coming from WTI and new Asian benchmarks. Brent is increasingly tethered to a shrinking base of North Sea output, forcing Basket methodology adjustments to paper over declining volumes. This risks pricing anomalies, discourages global macro and systematic flows, and erodes Brent\u2019s network effects.\n\n - *Even major Asian refiners are now referencing Oman and Shanghai benchmarks for key deals\u2014a dilution of Brent\u2019s iron grip on global trade.*\n\n- **Liquidity In Long-Dated Contracts Is Abysmal.** \n Deferred Brent futures show declining open interest and thinner spreads. Programmatic/CTA adoption lags WTI, hampering the efficient implementation of systematic trend or mean-reversion models. This isn\u2019t academic: thinning liquidity *magnifies volatility, widens spreads, and raises the risk of price dislocations*.\n\n - **Lesson:** In the late 2010s, as WTI microstructure improved, money flowed away from Brent in hotly traded contracts. Fundamentals *moved markets*, not merely \u201clegacy benchmark\u201d status.\n\n---\n\n# IV. If you want to depend on a \u201cfloor\u201d from a cartel increasingly fractured by Russia\u2019s and smaller African members\u2019 non-compliance, or by global demand headwinds, don\u2019t be surprised when the market breaks through.\n\n - **Lesson:** I once mistook the OPEC+ floor in 2018\u20132019 for a base, only to watch repeated, failure-prone vows to \u201cdefend price\u201d result in steady erosion below $60.\n\n- **Event Risk is Two-Edged\u2014It Is Already Priced and Fades Fast.** \n Current premiums for geopolitical events have proven *ephemeral*. When VLCC shipping panics washed out, the risk premium vanished and prices retreated. Betting on further escalation is a lottery, not a repeatable process: the market *dumps* these premiums fast.\n\n---\n\n# V. If this is the beginning of a regime shift, not a temporary pop, you\u2019re essentially standing in front of a freight train while volatility is still expanding. Yes\u2014event-driven spikes present opportunity\u2014but waiting for failed breakouts or confirmed reversals gives you better odds than full conviction shorts into what might be only the first leg of a bull reversal.\n\nTo the Safe Analyst: \nYou make a strong case for capital preservation, and yes, ignoring the reality of high inventories and cautious long-term forecasts is shortsighted. Waiting for multiple weeks of inventory draws or a \u201cquiet\u201d confirmation could easily see Brent at $70+ before slower money gets involved. At that point, the risk/reward for new shorts is actually much worse.\n\nAlso, while you\u2019re correct that options hedging has become expensive, you overlook the potential benefits of *selectively* monetizing elevated implied volatility\u2014there are ways to structure options spreads or collars that protect against event spikes without bleeding premium in a sideways grind.\n\nWhere Both Arguments Fall Short\u2014and What a Balanced Path Looks Like: \nNeither \u201caggressive short here\u201d nor \u201ctotal risk-off\u201d is optimal. There\u2019s a time to size up and a time to reduce exposure, but the present signal is mixed: short-term and medium-term price action has flipped bullish, social sentiment has revived, and inventory and long-term supply/demand suggest any strength will eventually be capped.\n\nThe moderate, **sustainable** play is to:\n\n- **Size down the outright short.** If you want to express the bearish supply case, do it with partial exposure\u2014don\u2019t go full conviction until (a) price loses the 10- and 50-day averages, and/or (b) the next weekly inventory data confirms a resumption of builds or a failed draw. \n- **Use option hedges, but favor defined-risk structures.** Protect against near-term spikes by using tight, cost-effective puts to limit mark-to-market risk instead of \u201copen-ended\u201d short deltas. Option spreads/collars involving both calls and puts keep hedging costs manageable while protecting exposure. \n- **Explore calendar or pairs trades with less outright directionality.** A short calendar spread or a pairs trade versus a more supply-constrained product (e.g., jet fuel or products with bullish physical setups) enables you to stay positioned for curve normalization and structural weakness if supply reasserts itself, while reducing outright directional pain. \n- **Let trend-following signals guide reversals.** If price closes below the 62.50\u201363 level on a daily basis and MACD/RSI momentum turns down, scale into your short. If price holds the 10- and 50-day averages and momentum improves, reduce bearish bias and look for more neutral/long-biased set-ups. \n- **Keep liquidity and event monitoring at the front of your process.** With GPRD_THREAT and OVX bouncing all over, position-sizing discipline and speed of response are critical\u2014you must be ready to either cut risk or flip with fresh news. No set-and-forget.\n\n**In summary:** \nThe best approach blends the Risky Analyst\u2019s tactical opportunism **with** the Safe Analyst\u2019s appreciation for regime risks and capital protection. Take a starter short, but with moderate size and robust, *cost-effective* options protection. Be ready to add if the macro/fundamental picture turns further bearish and technicals confirm. But equally, don\u2019t ignore fresh uptrends\u2014if price holds and squeezes higher on further risk, be nimble and cut back.\n\nDon\u2019t just fade price or hide in your shell: stay active, keep risk scalable, and pivot as confirmation or invalidation emerges. ## 1. ì‹œì¥ ê°œìš”

ìµœê·¼ 1ê°œì›”(25.12.27~26.01.26) ê´€ì¸¡ êµ¬ê°„ì—ì„œ ë¸Œë ŒíŠ¸ìœ ëŠ” ì§€ì •í•™Â·í•´ìƒë¬¼ë¥˜ ì´ìŠˆê°€ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì„ í”ë“¤ì—ˆì§€ë§Œ, ê¸°ê´€ ì „ë§ì—ì„œ ë°˜ë³µì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì–¸ê¸‰ë˜ëŠ” 2026ë…„ ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ ì™€ ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•˜ëŠ” íë¦„ìœ¼ë¡œ ì •ë¦¬ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[1][2]. ê°€ì¥ ìµœê·¼ ì£¼ê°„ êµ¬ê°„(01.19~01.23)ì—ì„œëŠ” í•´ìƒ ìš´ì„ì´ í° í­ìœ¼ë¡œ ë˜ëŒë¦¼ì„ ë³´ì´ë©° ë¬¼ë¥˜ë°œ ë¹„ìš© ì••ë ¥ì´ ì™„í™”ë˜ëŠ” ì¡°ì§ì´ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚¬ê³ , ë™ì‹œì— ë³€ë™ì„±ì´ ì¬í™•ëŒ€ë˜ë©° ë°©í–¥ì„±ë³´ë‹¤ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ ë‚¨ëŠ” êµ­ë©´ìœ¼ë¡œ ê´€ì¸¡ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[8]. ì´ëŸ¬í•œ ì¡°í•©ì€ â€œì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì„± í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì˜ íŒ½ì°½ê³¼ ìˆ˜ì¶•â€ì´ ì§§ì€ ì£¼ê¸°ì— ë°˜ë³µë˜ëŠ” ê°€ìš´ë°, êµ¬ì¡°ì  ìš”ì¸(ì¬ê³ Â·ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ )ì´ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì˜ í•˜ë°©ì„ ì§€ì§€í•˜ëŠ” í˜•íƒœë¡œ í•´ì„ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[1][4].

## 2. ì£¼ìš” ìš”ì¸ ë¶„ì„

### 2-1. í•˜ë½ ìš”ì¸ â€“ ìˆ˜ê¸‰(í€ë”ë©˜í„¸)

ì´ëŸ¬í•œ êµ¬ì¡°ëŠ” ë¯¸êµ­ ì—ë„ˆì§€ì •ë³´ì²­(EIA) ì „ë§ì—ì„œë„ ìœ ì‚¬í•˜ê²Œ ê´€ì¸¡ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. EIAëŠ” ë‹¨ê¸°ì „ë§(Short-Term Energy Outlook) ê´€ë ¨ ê³µê°œ ìë£Œì—ì„œ 2026ë…„ìœ¼ë¡œ ê°ˆìˆ˜ë¡ ë¹„OPEC ìƒì‚° ì¦ê°€ ë“±ì´ ê°€ê²©ì˜ ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ë©”ì‹œì§€ë¥¼ ì œì‹œí•˜ê³  ìˆìœ¼ë©°(2025-12-09), ì´ëŠ” â€œê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ë ¥â€ì´ í•˜ë½ ë…¼ë¦¬ì˜ í•µì‹¬ ì¶•ìœ¼ë¡œ ìœ ì§€ë¨ì„ ë’·ë°›ì¹¨í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[3].

ìµœê·¼ 1ê°œì›” ê´€ì¸¡ êµ¬ê°„ì˜ ë‰´ìŠ¤ íë¦„ì—ì„œë„ â€œê³µê¸‰ì´ ë„‰ë„‰í•˜ê³  ìˆ˜ìš”ê°€ ê°•í•˜ê²Œ ë°›ì³ì£¼ì§€ ëª»í•œë‹¤â€ëŠ” í†¤ì´ ë°˜ë³µë©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¡œì´í„°ëŠ” 2026-01-05 ë³´ë„ì—ì„œ ê³µê¸‰ì´ ì¶©ë¶„í•˜ê³  ìˆ˜ìš” ì¸¡ ì‹ í˜¸ê°€ ì•½í•´ì§ˆ ë•Œ ìœ ê°€ê°€ í•˜ë½ ì••ë ¥ì„ ë°›ì„ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ì‹œì¥ ë§¥ë½ì„ ì „í–ˆê³ , ì´ëŠ” ë‹¨ê¸° ë°˜ë“±ì´ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚˜ë”ë¼ë„ ì§€ì†ì„±ì´ ì œí•œë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[4].

ë˜í•œ 2026-01-13 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œëŠ” ì¬ê³  ì¦ê°€(ë¯¸êµ­ ì¬ê³  ìš”ì¸ ë“±)ê°€ ê°€ê²©ì˜ ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•˜ëŠ” ì¬ë£Œë¡œ í•¨ê»˜ ì–¸ê¸‰ë˜ë©°, ìˆ˜ê¸‰ ì¸¡ë©´ì—ì„œ â€œì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ë‚¨ì•„ ìˆëŠ” ìƒíƒœâ€ë¼ëŠ” í•´ì„ì´ ê°•í™”ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[6]. ì¢…í•©í•˜ë©´, ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ê°€ ë°œìƒí•˜ë”ë¼ë„ í€ë”ë©˜í„¸ì˜ êµ¬ì¡°ì  íƒ€ì´íŠ¸ë‹ ì‹ í˜¸ê°€ ì•½í•˜ë©´ í•˜ë½ ì••ë ¥ì´ ì™„ë§Œí•˜ê²Œ ìš°ì„¸í•´ì§ˆ ì—¬ì§€ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-13)[6].

### 2-2. í•˜ë½ ìš”ì¸ â€“ ë§¤í¬ë¡œ

ë§¤í¬ë¡œ í™˜ê²½ì—ì„œëŠ” â€œìˆ˜ìš” ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ê³µê¸‰ ì¦ê°€ë¥¼ ì¶©ë¶„íˆ í¡ìˆ˜í•˜ì§€ ëª»í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤â€ëŠ” ìš°ë ¤ê°€ í•˜ë½ ë…¼ë¦¬ë¥¼ ë³´ê°•í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. IEAëŠ” 2026ë…„ ìˆ˜ìš” ì¦ê°€ì™€ ê³µê¸‰ ì¦ê°€ì˜ ê· í˜•ì´ ê³µê¸‰ ìš°ìœ„ë¡œ ê¸°ìš¸ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ê´€ì ì„ ì œì‹œí•˜ë©°(2026-01-21), ìˆ˜ìš” ì¸¡ ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ê°•í•˜ê²Œ íšŒë³µë˜ì§€ ì•Šì„ ê²½ìš° ê°€ê²©ì´ ì¬ê³ Â·ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ ì— ë” ë¯¼ê°í•˜ê²Œ ë°˜ì‘í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[1].

ì‹œì¥ ê¸°ëŒ€ í˜•ì„± ê³¼ì •ì—ì„œëŠ” ì£¼ìš” ê¸ˆìœµê¸°ê´€ ì „ë§ ì¡°ì •ì´ ë‹¨ê¸° ì‹¬ë¦¬ë¥¼ í”ë“œëŠ” ë³€ìˆ˜ë¡œ ì‘ë™í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¡œì´í„°ëŠ” 2026-01-12 ë³´ë„ì—ì„œ ì£¼ìš” IBì˜ ì „ë§ ì¡°ì • ì´ìŠˆë¥¼ ì „í•˜ë©°, ìˆ˜ìš”Â·ì •ì±…Â·ê°€ê²© ë°¸ëŸ°ìŠ¤ì— ëŒ€í•œ ì‹œì¥ì˜ ë³´ìˆ˜ì  í•´ì„ì´ í™•ì‚°ë  ë•Œ ìœ ê°€ ìƒë‹¨ì´ ì œí•œë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ë³´ì—¬ì¤ë‹ˆë‹¤[5].

ê¸ˆìœµì‹œì¥ ë³€ë™ì„± ì¸¡ë©´ì—ì„œë„ â€œìœ„í—˜íšŒí”¼ê°€ ê°•í•´ì§€ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„â€ì€ ì›ìœ ë¥¼ í¬í•¨í•œ ê²½ê¸°ë¯¼ê° ìì‚°ì˜ ìƒë°©ì„ ì œì•½í•˜ê¸° ì‰½ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¡œì´í„°ëŠ” 2026-01-16 ê¸€ë¡œë²Œ ë§ˆì¼“ ë³´ë„ì—ì„œ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„± í™•ëŒ€ êµ­ë©´ì—ì„œ ì•ˆì „ìì‚° ì„ í˜¸ê°€ ë¶€ê°ë˜ëŠ” íë¦„ì„ ì „í–ˆê³ , ê°™ì€ ë§¥ë½ì—ì„œ ìœ ê°€ëŠ” ë‹¨ê¸° ìˆì»¤ë²„ë¡œ ì§€ì§€ë°›ì„ ìˆ˜ ìˆì–´ë„ ë§¤í¬ë¡œ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ ë‚¨ìœ¼ë©´ ì¶”ì„¸ì  ê°•ì„¸ë¡œ ì´ì–´ì§€ê¸° ì–´ë µë‹¤ëŠ” í•´ì„ì´ ê°€ëŠ¥í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[8].

ë˜í•œ ì—°ë§Â·ì—°ì´ˆ êµ¬ê°„ì˜ ì‹œì¥ ë¶„ìœ„ê¸°ë¥¼ ë‹¤ë£¬ 2026-01-02 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œë„ ê±°ì‹œÂ·ì •ì±… ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ ìœ„í—˜ìì‚° ì „ë°˜ì˜ ê°€ê²© í˜•ì„±ì— ì˜í–¥ì„ ì¤€ë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì´ ì–¸ê¸‰ë˜ë©°, ì›ìœ ë„ ì˜ˆì™¸ê°€ ì•„ë‹ˆë¼ëŠ” ì ì´ í™•ì¸ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[9]. ê²°ê³¼ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë§¤í¬ë¡œëŠ” â€œì™„ë§Œí•œ í•˜ë½ ìš°ì„¸â€ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ë¥¼ ë’·ë°›ì¹¨í•˜ë˜, ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ ë°œìƒ ì‹œ ë‹¨ê¸° ë³€ë™ì„±ì€ ë³‘ì¡´í•˜ëŠ” êµ¬ì¡°ë¡œ í‰ê°€ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-16)[8].

### 2-3. í•˜ë½ ìš”ì¸ â€“ ì§€ì •í•™

ì§€ì •í•™ì€ ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ë§Œë“¤ ìˆ˜ ìˆì§€ë§Œ, ìµœê·¼ 1ê°œì›” ê´€ì¸¡ êµ¬ê°„ì—ì„œëŠ” â€œë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ê³µê¸‰ ì°¨ì§ˆì˜ ì§€ì†ì„±â€ë³´ë‹¤ â€œì‹¬ë¦¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì˜ ê°€ë³€ì„±â€ì´ ë” í¬ê²Œ ê´€ì¸¡ë˜ëŠ” íë¦„ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. IEAëŠ” 2026ë…„ ì´ˆ ìˆ˜ê¸‰ì„ ë…¼ì˜í•˜ëŠ” ê³¼ì •ì—ì„œ ì§€ì •í•™ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ê°€ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì„ í”ë“¤ ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë‚˜, êµ¬ì¡°ì  ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ ê°€ ì»¤ì§ˆ ê²½ìš° í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ í¬ì„ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-21)[1].

01ì›” ì¤‘ìˆœ êµ¬ê°„ì—ëŠ” í•´ìƒ ìš´ì†¡Â·ì§€ì •í•™ ë‰´ìŠ¤ê°€ ìœ ê°€ë¥¼ ì§€ì§€í•˜ëŠ” ì¬ë£Œë¡œ ì‘ë™í•œ ì •í™©ì´ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. 2026-01-15 ë¡œì´í„°ëŠ” íŠ¹ì • ì§€ì—­ ì •ì„¸ ë° ê³µê¸‰ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ë¥¼ ë‘˜ëŸ¬ì‹¼ ìš°ë ¤ê°€ ìœ ê°€ì— ì˜í–¥ì„ ì¤„ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ë§¥ë½ì„ ì „í–ˆìœ¼ë‚˜, ë™ì‹œì— ì´ëŸ¬í•œ ì¬ë£Œê°€ í€ë”ë©˜í„¸ì„ ê·¼ë³¸ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë°”ê¾¸ê¸°ë³´ë‹¤ â€œë‹¨ê¸° ì‹¬ë¦¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„â€ ì„±ê²©ì´ ê°•í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ í•¨ê»˜ ê³ ë ¤í•  í•„ìš”ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤[7]. ì´ì™€ ê°™ì€ ë§¥ë½ì—ì„œ ê³ ì¶©ê²© ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì˜ ì„¸ë¶€ ì‚¬ì‹¤ê´€ê³„ëŠ” ë‹¨ì¼ ë³´ë„ë§Œìœ¼ë¡œ ë‹¨ì •í•˜ê¸°ë³´ë‹¤, ë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ì°¨ì§ˆê³¼ ì‹¬ë¦¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ë¶„ë¦¬í•´ í•´ì„í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ ì ì ˆí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-15)[7].

ê°€ì¥ ìµœê·¼ ì£¼ê°„(01.19~01.23) ì…ë ¥ íë¦„ì—ì„œ í•´ìƒ ìš´ì„ì´ ë˜ëŒë¦¼ì„ ë³´ì¸ ì ì€ â€œë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ë³‘ëª©â€ì´ ì™„í™”ë  ë•Œ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ì¶•ì†Œë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•˜ë©°, ì´ëŠ” í•˜ë½ ë…¼ë¦¬ì™€ ë§ë¬¼ë¦½ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¡œì´í„° 2026-01-16 ë³´ë„ì—ì„œëŠ” ê³µê¸‰ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ ìš°ë ¤ê°€ ë‚¨ì•„ ìˆì–´ë„ ë‹¨ê¸° í¬ì§€ì…˜ ì •ë¦¬(ìˆì»¤ë²„) ë“±ìœ¼ë¡œ ê°€ê²©ì´ ì¼ì‹œì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì§€ì§€ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ì •í™©ì´ ì–¸ê¸‰ë˜ë©°, ì§€ì •í•™ì´ â€˜ë°©í–¥ì„±â€™ë³´ë‹¤ëŠ” â€˜ë³€ë™ì„±â€™ì— ë” í° ì˜í–¥ì„ ì£¼ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„ìœ¼ë¡œ í•´ì„ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[8].

## 3. ì œí•œì  ìƒìŠ¹ ìš”ì¸

í•˜ë½ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ì—ì„œë„ â€œì œí•œì  ë°˜ë“±â€ì„ ë§Œë“¤ ìˆ˜ ìˆëŠ” ìš”ì¸ì€ ì¡´ì¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì²«ì§¸ë¡œ, ì§€ì •í•™Â·í•´ìš´ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ëŠ” ì‚¬ê±´ ë°œìƒ ì‹œì ì— ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ì¬í˜•ì„±í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë©°, ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ê°€ê²©ì„ ì§€ì§€í•˜ëŠ” ë°©í–¥ìœ¼ë¡œ ì‘ë™í•  ì—¬ì§€ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-15)[7]. ë‹¤ë§Œ IEAê°€ 2026ë…„ ì´ˆ ê³µê¸‰ ìš°ìœ„ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì„ ê°•ì¡°í•˜ëŠ” í™˜ê²½ì—ì„œëŠ”, í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ í™•ëŒ€ë˜ë”ë¼ë„ ì§€ì†ì„±ì´ ì§§ì•„ì§ˆ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ìˆì–´ ê²°ê³¼ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ìƒìŠ¹ ì••ë ¥ì€ ì œí•œì ì¸ ìš”ì¸ìœ¼ë¡œ í‰ê°€ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-21)[1].

ë‘˜ì§¸ë¡œ, ì‹œì¥ í¬ì§€ì…”ë‹ ìš”ì¸ì€ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì˜ íƒ„ë ¥ì„ ì¢Œìš°í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. 2026-01-16 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œ ì–¸ê¸‰ë˜ë“¯ì´, ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ìˆì»¤ë²„ê°€ ìœ ê°€ë¥¼ ì§€ì§€í•˜ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„ì´ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚  ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë©° ì´ëŠ” â€œì¼ì‹œì  ë°˜ë“±â€ì˜ ê²½ë¡œê°€ ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[8]. ë‹¤ë§Œ 2026-01-13 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œì²˜ëŸ¼ ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•˜ëŠ” ì¬ë£Œë¡œ ì‘ë™í•˜ëŠ” êµ­ë©´ì—ì„œëŠ”, ë°˜ë“±ì´ ì¶”ì„¸ì  ê°•ì„¸ë¡œ ì „í™˜ë˜ê¸°ë³´ë‹¤ëŠ” ì œí•œì  ë²”ìœ„ì—ì„œ ì†Œí™”ë  ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤[6].

## 4. ì‹œì¥ í•´ì„ ë° ì‹œì‚¬ì 

ì¢…í•©í•˜ë©´, í–¥í›„ 1ì£¼ì¼ ë¸Œë ŒíŠ¸ìœ  ì‹œì¥ì€ ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ ì™€ ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ë¼ëŠ” êµ¬ì¡°ì  í•˜ë°© ìš”ì¸ì´ ìš°ì„¸í•œ ê°€ìš´ë°, ì§€ì •í•™Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜ ë‰´ìŠ¤ì— ë”°ë¥¸ ë‹¨ê¸° ë³€ë™ì„±ì´ ë³‘ì¡´í•˜ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„ìœ¼ë¡œ í‰ê°€ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[1][2]. ë¬¼ë¥˜ ì¸¡ë©´ì—ì„œëŠ” â€œì°¨ì§ˆì˜ í˜„ì‹¤í™”â€ì™€ â€œì •ìƒí™” ì‹ í˜¸â€ê°€ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ êµì°¨í•œë‹¤. ìµœê·¼ì—ëŠ” í™í•´ í•­ë¡œ ê´€ë ¨ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ ì™„í™”ë˜ë©° ì£¼ìš” ì„ ì‚¬ë“¤ì˜ ìš´í•­ ì¬ê°œ ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ë¶€ê°ë˜ëŠ” ë“±, ìš´ì„ ê¸‰ë“± êµ¬ê°„ì—ì„œ í˜•ì„±ëœ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ì¶•ì†Œë  ì—¬ì§€ê°€ ê´€ì¸¡ëœë‹¤[5]. ì´ëŠ” 01/19 â†’ 01/23ì— ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚œ ìš´ì„ ê¸‰ë½(íŒ¨ë‹‰ ì™„í™”)ê³¼ë„ ì •í•©ì ì´ë©°, 1ê°œì›” ê´€ì ì—ì„œ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì˜ ìƒì‹œí™”ë³´ë‹¤ëŠ” â€˜ê¸‰ë“± í›„ ë˜ëŒë¦¼â€™ íŒ¨í„´ì´ ìš°ì„¸í•  ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì„ ë†’ì¸ë‹¤.

ê±°ì‹œ í™˜ê²½ì€ ìˆ˜ìš”ì˜ â€œê°•í•œ íšŒë³µâ€ì„ ì „ì œí•˜ê¸° ì–´ë µë‹¤ëŠ” ìª½ìœ¼ë¡œ ê¸°ìš¸ì–´ ì•½ì„¸ë¥¼ ë³´ê°•í•œë‹¤. ### 2-3. 1ê°œì›” ì „ë§(Forward)

ë² ì´ìŠ¤ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ì—ì„œ í–¥í›„ 1ê°œì›” ë¸Œë ŒíŠ¸ìœ ëŠ” ì™„ë§Œí•œ í•˜ë½ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ìš°ì„¸í•˜ë‹¤. ìµœê·¼ 4ì£¼ íë¦„ì—ì„œ ì§€ì •í•™Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜ ì´ìŠˆê°€ ë‹¨ê¸° ê¸‰ë“±ì„ ë§Œë“¤ì—ˆì§€ë§Œ, ê·¸ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ìš´ì„ ê¸‰ë½ê³¼ í•¨ê»˜ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ ë˜ëŒë¦¼ì„ ë³´ì˜€ê³ , ê¸°ê´€ ì „ë§ê³¼ í†µê³„ ìë£ŒëŠ” ë†’ì€ ì¬ê³  ë° 2026ë…„ ê³µê¸‰ ê³¼ì‰ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ê°€ê²© ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•˜ëŠ” í•µì‹¬ ë°°ê²½ì„ì„ ë°˜ë³µí•´ì„œ ì œì‹œí•œë‹¤[2][3][4]. ë”°ë¼ì„œ ë‹¨ê¸° ë°˜ë“±ì´ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚˜ë”ë¼ë„ â€œì‹¤ë¬¼ ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ë‚¨ì•„ ìˆëŠ” ìƒíƒœì—ì„œ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì„± í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ì¶•ì†Œë˜ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„â€ì—ì„œëŠ” í•˜ë°© ì••ë ¥ì´ ì ì§„ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ìš°ì„¸í•´ì§€ê¸° ì‰½ë‹¤.

ìˆ˜ê¸‰ ê²½ë¡œëŠ” â€œë‹¨ê¸° í”ë“¤ë¦¼ì€ ìˆë˜ êµ¬ì¡°ë¥¼ ë’¤ì§‘ê¸° ì–´ë µë‹¤â€ëŠ” í˜•íƒœê°€ ìœ ë ¥í•˜ë‹¤. 12/29 â†’ 01/02ì˜ ìˆ˜ì… ì¦ê°€(ì¬ê³  ì••ë ¥ í™•ëŒ€)ì™€ 01/19 â†’ 01/23ì˜ ìˆ˜ì… ê°ì†Œ(ë‹¨ê¸° íƒ€ì´íŠ¸ë‹ ì‹ í˜¸)ê°€ êµì°¨í•˜ë“¯, ì£¼ê°„ ìˆ˜ì…Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜ì˜ ë³€í™”ëŠ” ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì„ í”ë“¤ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤. ê·¸ëŸ¬ë‚˜ ì¬ê³  ë ˆë²¨ì´ ë†’ì€ êµ­ë©´ì—ì„œëŠ” ë‹¨ê¸° íƒ€ì´íŠ¸ë‹ ì‹ í˜¸ê°€ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚˜ë„ â€˜ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì—´ì–´ì –í ë§Œí¼ì˜ ì—°ì†ì ì¸ í€ë”ë©˜í„¸ ê°œì„ â€™ìœ¼ë¡œ ì—°ê²°ë˜ê¸° ì–´ë ¤ìš°ë©°, ë°˜ë“±ì€ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ ì†Œë©¸ê³¼ í•¨ê»˜ ì¦ì€ ë˜ëŒë¦¼ì— ë…¸ì¶œëœë‹¤[3][4].

ì§€ì •í•™Â·OPEC+ ë³€ìˆ˜ëŠ” í•˜ë‹¨ì„ ë°›ì¹˜ëŠ” ì—­í• ì„ í•˜ë˜, 1ê°œì›” ì‹œê³„ì—ì„œ â€œìƒìŠ¹ ì¶”ì„¸ë¥¼ ë§Œë“¤ê¸° ìœ„í•œ ì¡°ê±´â€ì€ ê¹Œë‹¤ë¡­ë‹¤. ëŒ€ì´ë€ ì œì¬ ê°•í™”ì™€ ê°™ì€ ë‰´ìŠ¤ëŠ” ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ìˆœê°„ì ìœ¼ë¡œ í™•ëŒ€í•´ 65ë‹¬ëŸ¬ëŒ€ ì¤‘ë°˜ íšŒë³µì„ ê°€ëŠ¥í•˜ê²Œ í•˜ì§€ë§Œ[1], ì´ë¥¼ ì¶”ì„¸ë¡œ ì „í™˜ì‹œí‚¤ë ¤ë©´ ì‹¤ì œ ê³µê¸‰ ì°¨ì§ˆì˜ ì§€ì†ì„± ë˜ëŠ” ì¬ê³ ì˜ ì˜ë¯¸ ìˆëŠ” ê°ì†Œê°€ í™•ì¸ë˜ì–´ì•¼ í•œë‹¤. ë¬¼ë¥˜ ì¸¡ë©´ì—ì„œë„ í™í•´Â·ìˆ˜ì—ì¦ˆ ê´€ë ¨ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ì¬ì°¨ í™•ëŒ€ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë‚˜, ì •ìƒí™” ì‹ í˜¸ê°€ í•¨ê»˜ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚˜ëŠ” í™˜ê²½ì—ì„œëŠ” í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ìƒì‹œí™”ë˜ê¸°ë³´ë‹¤ëŠ” â€œê¸‰ë“±-ìˆ˜ì¶•â€ íŒ¨í„´ì„ ë°˜ë³µí•  ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ë†’ë‹¤[5].

ì¢…í•©í•˜ë©´, í–¥í›„ 1ê°œì›”ì€ â€œë†’ì€ ì¬ê³ Â·ê³µê¸‰ ê³¼ì‰ ì „ë§â€ì´ ì¤‘ê¸° ì•µì»¤ë¡œ ì‘ë™í•˜ëŠ” ê°€ìš´ë°, â€œë¬¼ë¥˜Â·ì§€ì •í•™ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì˜ ë¹ ë¥¸ íŒ½ì°½ê³¼ ìˆ˜ì¶•â€ì´ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì„ í”ë“¤ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ í¬ë‹¤. ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ê°€ í•˜ë‹¨ì„ ì§€ì§€í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë‚˜, ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ í•´ì†Œë˜ì§€ ì•ŠëŠ” í•œ ë°˜ë“±ì˜ ì§€ì†ì„±ì€ ì œí•œë  ê³µì‚°ì´ í¬ë‹¤[2][3][4]. ë‹¤ë§Œ ì§€ì •í•™ ì¶©ê²©ì˜ ê°•ë„ì™€ ì‹¤ë¬¼ ì°¨ì§ˆ ì—¬ë¶€ì— ë”°ë¼ ë°˜ëŒ€ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ê°€ êµ¬ê°„ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚  ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì€ ì—´ì–´ë‘˜ í•„ìš”ê°€ ìˆë‹¤.

## 3. ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ ìš”ì¸

ìƒë°© ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ì˜ í•µì‹¬ì€ ì¤‘ë™ë°œ ê³ ì¶©ê²© ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì˜ í˜„ì‹¤í™”ë‹¤. ëŒ€ì´ë€ ì••ë°• ê°•í™”, ì œì¬ í™•ëŒ€, í•´ìƒ ì¶©ëŒ ë“±ì€ ê³µê¸‰ ì°¨ì§ˆ ìš°ë ¤ë¥¼ ì¦í­ì‹œí‚¤ë©° ë‹¨ê¸°ê°„ì— ê°€ê²©ì„ ëŒì–´ì˜¬ë¦´ ìˆ˜ ìˆê³ , ì‹¤ì œë¡œ 1ì›” í•˜ìˆœì—ë„ ì´ëŸ¬í•œ ì„±ê²©ì˜ ë‰´ìŠ¤ê°€ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ì¬ì í™”í–ˆë‹¤[1]. ì—¬ê¸°ì— ì¹´ìíìŠ¤íƒ„ ë“± ë¹„OPEC ì£¼ìš” ì‚°ìœ êµ­ì˜ ê³µê¸‰ ì°¨ì§ˆì´ ë™ë°˜ë  ê²½ìš°, â€˜í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„â€™ì´ ì•„ë‹Œ â€˜ë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ë¬¼ëŸ‰â€™ ìš”ì¸ì´ ë˜ì–´ ìƒìŠ¹ ì••ë ¥ì´ ê°•í™”ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤[1].

ë˜ ë‹¤ë¥¸ ìƒë°© ìš”ì¸ì€ OPEC+ì˜ ë°©ì–´ ê°•ë„ë‹¤. ì¦ì‚° ì‹œì ì„ ëŠ¦ì¶”ê±°ë‚˜(í˜¹ì€ ê°ì‚°ì„ ê°•í™”í•˜ëŠ”) ì •ì±…ì´ ìœ ì§€ë˜ë©´ í•˜ë‹¨ ë°©ì–´ëŠ” ê°€ëŠ¥í•˜ì§€ë§Œ, ì´ëŠ” ë™ì‹œì— â€œê³µê¸‰ ê³¼ì‰ ìš°ë ¤ê°€ í¬ë‹¤â€ëŠ” ì—­ì‹ í˜¸ë¡œë„ ì½í ìˆ˜ ìˆì–´ ë°©í–¥ì„± íš¨ê³¼ëŠ” ì œí•œì ì¼ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤[8]. ê²°êµ­ ìƒë°© ì¶”ì„¸ ì „í™˜ì„ ìœ„í•´ì„œëŠ” ì •ì±… ë°©ì–´ë§Œìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ë¶€ì¡±í•˜ê³ , ì¬ê³ ì˜ ì²´ê³„ì  ê°ì†Œ ë˜ëŠ” ìˆ˜ìš”ì˜ ì˜ˆìƒ ë°– ë°˜ë“±ì´ í•„ìš”í•˜ë‹¤.

í•˜ë°© ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ëŠ” â€˜ì¬ê³ Â·ê³µê¸‰ ê³¼ì‰ ì „ë§â€™ì˜ ì¬ê°•í™”ì™€ ìˆ˜ìš” ê¸°ëŒ€ì˜ ë‘”í™”ë‹¤. EIAì™€ IEA ë“± ê¸°ê´€ ì „ë§ì´ ê³µê¸‰-ìˆ˜ìš” ë°¸ëŸ°ìŠ¤ì˜ ëŠìŠ¨í•¨ì„ ê°•ì¡°í•˜ëŠ” ê°€ìš´ë°[2][3], ì£¼ê°„ í†µê³„ì—ì„œë„ ì¬ê³  ìƒë‹¨ ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ìœ ì§€ë˜ë©´, ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì„± ë°˜ë“±ì´ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚˜ë„ ë˜ëŒë¦¼ì´ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ ë°œìƒí•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤[4]. ë˜í•œ ì„¸ê³„ ì„±ì¥ ê²½ë¡œê°€ ì™„ë§Œí•œ í™•ì¥ì— ë¨¸ë¬´ë¥´ê±°ë‚˜ í•˜ë°© ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ê°€ ë¶€ê°ë  ê²½ìš°, ê³ ì¬ê³  êµ­ë©´ì˜ ìœ ê°€ëŠ” ìˆ˜ìš” ê¸°ëŒ€ ë³€í™”ì— ë¯¼ê°í•˜ê²Œ ë°˜ì‘í•˜ë©° í•˜ë°© ë³€ë™ì„±ì´ ì»¤ì§ˆ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤[6][7].

ë¬¼ë¥˜ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì˜ ì •ìƒí™”ë„ í•˜ë°© ìš”ì¸ì´ë‹¤. í™í•´ í•­ë¡œ ê´€ë ¨ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ ì™„í™”ë˜ê³  ìš´í•­ ì¬ê°œ ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ê°•í™”ë˜ë©´, ìš´ì„ ê¸‰ë“±ì„ í†µí•´ í˜•ì„±ëœ â€˜ë¬¼ë¥˜ë°œ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„â€™ì´ ì¶•ì†Œë˜ë©° ê°€ê²© ìƒë‹¨ì´ ë”ìš± ì œí•œë  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤[5]. ë”°ë¼ì„œ 1ê°œì›” êµ¬ê°„ì€ â€œë°©í–¥ì„±ì€ ì™„ë§Œí•œ í•˜ë°©, ë³€ë™ì„±ì€ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì— ì˜í•´ ê°„í—ì ìœ¼ë¡œ í™•ëŒ€â€ë˜ëŠ” ì¡°í•©ì´ ê¸°ë³¸ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ë¡œ ì í•©í•˜ë‹¤.

## 4. ê²°ë¡ 

ìµœê·¼ 4ì£¼ íë¦„ì€ ì§€ì •í•™Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜ ìš”ì¸ìœ¼ë¡œ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ê¸‰íŒ½ì°½í–ˆë‹¤ê°€, ìš´ì„ ì •ìƒí™” ì‹ í˜¸ì™€ í•¨ê»˜ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ ìˆ˜ì¶•í•˜ëŠ” íŒ¨í„´ìœ¼ë¡œ ìš”ì•½ëœë‹¤. ì´ ê³¼ì •ì—ì„œ ë¯¸êµ­ ìˆ˜ì…, ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´, 2026ë…„ ê³µê¸‰ ê³¼ì‰ ì „ë§ì´ ê°€ê²© ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•˜ëŠ” ì¤‘ê¸° ì•µì»¤ë¡œ ì‘ë™í–ˆê³ , ê²°ê³¼ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë‹¨ê¸° ë°˜ë“±ì´ ìˆì–´ë„ ì¶”ì„¸ì  ê°•ì„¸ë¡œ ì´ì–´ì§€ê¸° ì–´ë ¤ìš´ í™˜ê²½ì´ ê°•í™”ë˜ì—ˆë‹¤[2][3][4].

ë”°ë¼ì„œ í–¥í›„ 1ê°œì›”ì˜ ê¸°ë³¸ íŒë‹¨ì€ â€œì™„ë§Œí•œ í•˜ë½ ìš°ì„¸â€ë‹¤. ë‹¤ë§Œ ì´ë€Â·í™í•´ ë“± ì§€ì •í•™ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ê°€ ì¬ì°¨ í™•ëŒ€ë  ê²½ìš° ë‹¨ê¸° ê¸‰ë“±ì€ ê°€ëŠ¥í•˜ë©°, ê·¸ ê¸‰ë“±ì˜ ì§€ì†ì„±ì€ â€˜ì‹¤ë¬¼ ê³µê¸‰ ì°¨ì§ˆì˜ í˜„ì‹¤í™”â€™ì™€ â€˜ì¬ê³ ì˜ ì˜ë¯¸ ìˆëŠ” ê°ì†Œâ€™ ì—¬ë¶€ì— ì˜í•´ ê²°ì •ë  ê²ƒì´ë‹¤[1][4]. ìš´ì„ ë° ì§€ì •í•™ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ì¬ì°¨ í™•ëŒ€ë˜ë”ë¼ë„, ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ìœ ì§€ë˜ëŠ” í•œ ë°˜ë“±ì˜ ì²´ë ¥ì€ ì œí•œë˜ëŠ” ìª½ì— ë¬´ê²Œë¥¼ ë‘”ë‹¤.

ë³¸ ë³´ê³ ì„œëŠ” ê³µê°œëœ ìë£Œì™€ ë‚´ë¶€ ì…ë ¥ ë°ì´í„°ë¥¼ ë°”íƒ•ìœ¼ë¡œ ìƒì„±í˜• AIë¥¼ í™œìš©í•´ ì´ˆì•ˆì„ ì‘ì„±í–ˆìœ¼ë©°, ìˆ˜ì¹˜Â·ì‚¬ì‹¤ê´€ê³„ëŠ” ì›ë¬¸ ì¶œì²˜ë¥¼ ìš°ì„ í•œë‹¤[IA1].

2. ì£¼ìš” ìš”ì¸ ë¶„ì„

EIAëŠ” ë‹¨ê¸°ì „ë§(Short-Term Energy Outlook) ê´€ë ¨ ê³µê°œ ìë£Œì—ì„œ 2026ë…„ìœ¼ë¡œ ê°ˆìˆ˜ë¡ ë¹„OPEC ìƒì‚° ì¦ê°€ ë“±ì´ ê°€ê²©ì˜ ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ë©”ì‹œì§€ë¥¼ ì œì‹œí•˜ê³  ìˆìœ¼ë©°(2025-12-09), ì´ëŠ” â€œê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ë ¥â€ì´ í•˜ë½ ë…¼ë¦¬ì˜ í•µì‹¬ ì¶•ìœ¼ë¡œ ìœ ì§€ë¨ì„ ë’·ë°›ì¹¨í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[3].

ìµœê·¼ 1ê°œì›” ê´€ì¸¡ êµ¬ê°„ì—ì„œì˜ ì£¼ê°„ ë°ì´í„° ì—­ì‹œ â€œì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì™€ í€ë”ë©˜í„¸ì´ ì„œë¡œ ë‹¤ë¥¸ ë°©í–¥ì˜ ì‹ í˜¸ë¥¼ ë‚¼ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤â€ëŠ” ì ì„ ë³´ì—¬ì¤ë‹ˆë‹¤. 12.29~01.02ì— ë¯¸êµ­ ì›ìœ  ìˆ˜ì…(WCRIMUS2)ì´ 5.6% ì¦ê°€í•œ ì ì€ ë‹¨ê¸° ì¬ê³  ì••ë ¥ìœ¼ë¡œ ì—°ê²°ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆëŠ” ì•½ì„¸ ì¡°í•©ì¸ ë°˜ë©´, 01.19~01.23ì—ëŠ” ìˆ˜ì…ì´ 7.2% ê°ì†Œí•˜ë©° ë‹¨ê¸° ê³µê¸‰ íƒ€ì´íŠ¸ë‹ ì‹ í˜¸ê°€ ì„ì˜€ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë‹¤ë§Œ ìµœê·¼ 4ì£¼ì˜ ê³µí†µëœ ê²°ë¡ ì€, ìˆ˜ì…Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜ ë³€ìˆ˜ì˜ ë³€ë™ì´ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì„ í”ë“¤ë”ë¼ë„, ê¸°ê´€ ì „ë§ê³¼ ë‰´ìŠ¤ ìš”ì•½ì—ì„œ ë°˜ë³µë˜ëŠ” â€œê³µê¸‰ ìš°ìœ„Â·ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´â€ êµ¬ì¡°ë¥¼ ë’¤ì§‘ê¸°ì—ëŠ” ê·¼ê±°ê°€ ì œí•œì ì´ë¼ëŠ” ì ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤[1][4][10].

ë˜í•œ 2026-01-13 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œì²˜ëŸ¼ ì¬ê³  ì¦ê°€ ìš”ì¸ì´ ê°€ê²©ì˜ ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•˜ëŠ” ì¬ë£Œë¡œ í•¨ê»˜ ì–¸ê¸‰ë˜ë©°, ìˆ˜ê¸‰ ì¸¡ë©´ì—ì„œ â€œì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ë‚¨ì•„ ìˆëŠ” ìƒíƒœâ€ë¼ëŠ” í•´ì„ì´ ê°•í™”ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[6]. ì¢…í•©í•˜ë©´, ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ê°€ ë°œìƒí•˜ë”ë¼ë„ í€ë”ë©˜í„¸ì˜ êµ¬ì¡°ì  íƒ€ì´íŠ¸ë‹ ì‹ í˜¸ê°€ ì•½í•˜ë©´ í•˜ë½ ì••ë ¥ì´ ì™„ë§Œí•˜ê²Œ ìš°ì„¸í•´ì§ˆ ì—¬ì§€ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-13)[6].

2-2. í•˜ë½ ìš”ì¸ â€“ ë§¤í¬ë¡œ

ë§¤í¬ë¡œ í™˜ê²½ì—ì„œëŠ” â€œìˆ˜ìš” ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ê³µê¸‰ ì¦ê°€ë¥¼ ì¶©ë¶„íˆ í¡ìˆ˜í•˜ì§€ ëª»í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤â€ëŠ” ìš°ë ¤ê°€ í•˜ë½ ë…¼ë¦¬ë¥¼ ë³´ê°•í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. IEAëŠ” 2026ë…„ ìˆ˜ìš” ì¦ê°€ì™€ ê³µê¸‰ ì¦ê°€ì˜ ê· í˜•ì´ ê³µê¸‰ ìš°ìœ„ë¡œ ê¸°ìš¸ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ê´€ì ì„ ì œì‹œí•˜ë©°(2026-01-21), ìˆ˜ìš” ì¸¡ ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ê°•í•˜ê²Œ íšŒë³µë˜ì§€ ì•Šì„ ê²½ìš° ê°€ê²©ì´ ì¬ê³ Â·ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ ì— ë” ë¯¼ê°í•˜ê²Œ ë°˜ì‘í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[1].

ì‹œì¥ ê¸°ëŒ€ í˜•ì„± ê³¼ì •ì—ì„œëŠ” ì£¼ìš” ê¸ˆìœµê¸°ê´€ ì „ë§ ì¡°ì •ì´ ë‹¨ê¸° ì‹¬ë¦¬ë¥¼ í”ë“œëŠ” ë³€ìˆ˜ë¡œ ì‘ë™í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¡œì´í„°ëŠ” 2026-01-12 ë³´ë„ì—ì„œ ì£¼ìš” IBì˜ ì „ë§ ì¡°ì • ì´ìŠˆë¥¼ ì „í•˜ë©°, ìˆ˜ìš”Â·ì •ì±…Â·ê°€ê²© ë°¸ëŸ°ìŠ¤ì— ëŒ€í•œ ì‹œì¥ì˜ ë³´ìˆ˜ì  í•´ì„ì´ í™•ì‚°ë  ë•Œ ìœ ê°€ ìƒë‹¨ì´ ì œí•œë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ë³´ì—¬ì¤ë‹ˆë‹¤[5]. íŠ¹íˆ ì¬ê³ ê°€ ë†’ì€ êµ­ë©´ì—ì„œëŠ” ìˆ˜ìš” ê¸°ëŒ€ê°€ ì¡°ê¸ˆë§Œ í”ë“¤ë ¤ë„ ê°€ê²©ì´ ë¯¼ê°í•˜ê²Œ ì¡°ì •ìœ¼ë¡œ ë°˜ì‘í•˜ëŠ” ê²½í–¥ì´ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì—ì„œ, ì´ì™€ ê°™ì€ ì „ë§ ì¡°ì •ì€ ë‹¨ê¸° í•˜ë°©ì˜ ì´‰ë§¤ë¡œ ê¸°ëŠ¥í•  ì—¬ì§€ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤[5][10].

ê¸ˆìœµì‹œì¥ ë³€ë™ì„± ì¸¡ë©´ì—ì„œë„ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„± í™•ëŒ€ êµ¬ê°„ì€ ì›ìœ ë¥¼ í¬í•¨í•œ ê²½ê¸°ë¯¼ê° ìì‚°ì˜ ìƒë°©ì„ ì œì•½í•˜ê¸° ì‰½ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¡œì´í„°ëŠ” 2026-01-16 ê¸€ë¡œë²Œ ë§ˆì¼“ ë³´ë„ì—ì„œ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„± í™•ëŒ€ êµ­ë©´ì—ì„œ ì•ˆì „ìì‚° ì„ í˜¸ê°€ ë¶€ê°ë˜ëŠ” íë¦„ì„ ì „í–ˆê³ , ê°™ì€ ë§¥ë½ì—ì„œ ìœ ê°€ëŠ” ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì¼ì‹œì  ê¸°ìˆ ì  ë°˜ë“±ì´ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚˜ë”ë¼ë„ ë§¤í¬ë¡œ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ ë‚¨ìœ¼ë©´ ì¶”ì„¸ì  ê°•ì„¸ë¡œ ì´ì–´ì§€ê¸° ì–´ë µë‹¤ëŠ” í•´ì„ì´ ê°€ëŠ¥í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[8].

ë˜í•œ ì—°ë§Â·ì—°ì´ˆ êµ¬ê°„ì˜ ì‹œì¥ ë¶„ìœ„ê¸°ë¥¼ ë‹¤ë£¬ 2026-01-02 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œë„ ê±°ì‹œÂ·ì •ì±… ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ ìœ„í—˜ìì‚° ì „ë°˜ì˜ ê°€ê²© í˜•ì„±ì— ì˜í–¥ì„ ì¤€ë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì´ ì–¸ê¸‰ë˜ë©°, ì›ìœ ë„ ì˜ˆì™¸ê°€ ì•„ë‹ˆë¼ëŠ” ì ì´ í™•ì¸ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[9]. ê²°ê³¼ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë§¤í¬ë¡œëŠ” â€œì™„ë§Œí•œ í•˜ë½ ìš°ì„¸â€ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ë¥¼ ë’·ë°›ì¹¨í•˜ë˜, ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ ë°œìƒ ì‹œ ë‹¨ê¸° ë³€ë™ì„±ì€ ë³‘ì¡´í•˜ëŠ” êµ¬ì¡°ë¡œ í‰ê°€ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-16)[8].

2-3. í•˜ë½ ìš”ì¸ â€“ ì§€ì •í•™

ì§€ì •í•™ì€ ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ë§Œë“¤ ìˆ˜ ìˆì§€ë§Œ, ìµœê·¼ 1ê°œì›” ê´€ì¸¡ êµ¬ê°„ì—ì„œëŠ” â€œë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ê³µê¸‰ ì°¨ì§ˆì˜ ì§€ì†ì„±â€ë³´ë‹¤ â€œì‹¬ë¦¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì˜ ê°€ë³€ì„±â€ì´ ë” í¬ê²Œ ê´€ì¸¡ë˜ëŠ” íë¦„ì…ë‹ˆë‹¤. IEAëŠ” 2026ë…„ ì´ˆ ìˆ˜ê¸‰ì„ ë…¼ì˜í•˜ëŠ” ê³¼ì •ì—ì„œ ì§€ì •í•™ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ê°€ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²©ì„ í”ë“¤ ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë‚˜, êµ¬ì¡°ì  ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ ê°€ ì»¤ì§ˆ ê²½ìš° í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ë¹ ë¥´ê²Œ í¬ì„ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-21)[1].

01ì›” ì¤‘ìˆœ êµ¬ê°„ì—ëŠ” í•´ìƒ ìš´ì†¡Â·ì§€ì •í•™ ë‰´ìŠ¤ê°€ ìœ ê°€ë¥¼ ì§€ì§€í•˜ëŠ” ì¬ë£Œë¡œ ì‘ë™í•œ ì •í™©ì´ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. 01.12~01.16ì—ëŠ” VLCC ìš´ì„(D-AASFA00)ì´ 28.2% ìƒìŠ¹í•˜ê³  GPRD_THREATê°€ 23.7% ìƒìŠ¹í•˜ë©° í•´ìƒ ë¬¼ë¥˜ ì°¨ì§ˆ(ë¬¼ë¦¬)ê³¼ ìœ„í—˜ íšŒí”¼(ì‹¬ë¦¬)ê°€ ë™ì‹œì— ë¶€ê°ë˜ì—ˆê³ , ìš´ì„ ìƒìŠ¹ì´ ì •ì œë§ˆì§„ì„ í›¼ì†í•´ ìˆ˜ìš” ë‘”í™” ìš°ë ¤ë¥¼ ë™ë°˜í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì´ í•¨ê»˜ ì œì‹œë˜ì—ˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë‹¤ë§Œ ì´ êµ¬ê°„ì˜ íŠ¹ì„±ì€ â€œë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ì œì•½ê³¼ ì‹¬ë¦¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ë™ì‹œì— ì»¤ì¡Œìœ¼ë‚˜, ë¹„ìš© ìƒìŠ¹ì´ ìˆ˜ìš”ë¥¼ í›¼ì†í•  ê²½ìš° ì¤‘ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ì˜¤íˆë ¤ ì•½ì„¸ ìš”ì¸ìœ¼ë¡œ ì „í™˜ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤â€ëŠ” ì–‘ë©´ì„±ìœ¼ë¡œ í•´ì„ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤.

2026-01-15 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ëŠ” ì§€ì •í•™ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ê°€ ë‹¨ê¸° ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ í˜•ì„±í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ë³´ì—¬ì£¼ì§€ë§Œ, ë‹¨ì¼ ë³´ë„ë§Œìœ¼ë¡œ ì‚¬ê±´ì˜ íŒŒê¸‰ì„ ê³¼ë„í•˜ê²Œ ë‹¨ì •í•˜ê¸°ë³´ë‹¤ëŠ” ë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ì°¨ì§ˆê³¼ ì‹¬ë¦¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ë¶„ë¦¬í•´ í•´ì„í•˜ëŠ” ê²ƒì´ ì ì ˆí•©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-15)[7]. ì´ì™€ ê°™ì€ ë§¥ë½ì—ì„œ ê³ ì¶©ê²© ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì˜ ì„¸ë¶€ ì‚¬ì‹¤ê´€ê³„ëŠ”, ì¶”ê°€ì ì¸ ë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ì°¨ì§ˆ ì—¬ë¶€ê°€ í™•ì¸ë˜ëŠ”ì§€ì— ë”°ë¼ ìœ ê°€ ë°˜ì‘ì´ ë‹¬ë¼ì§ˆ ìˆ˜ ìˆë‹¤ëŠ” ì ì„ ì „ì œë¡œ í‰ê°€í•  í•„ìš”ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤[7].

ê°€ì¥ ìµœê·¼ ì£¼ê°„(01.19~01.23)ì—ì„œ VLCC ìš´ì„ì´ 41.6% í•˜ë½í•˜ë©° ë¬¼ë¥˜ë°œ ë¹„ìš© ì••ë ¥ì´ ë˜ëŒë¦¼ì„ ë³´ì¸ ì ì€ â€œë¬¼ë¦¬ì  ë³‘ëª©â€ì´ ì™„í™”ë  ë•Œ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ì¶•ì†Œë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•˜ë©°, ì´ëŠ” í•˜ë½ ë…¼ë¦¬ì™€ ë§ë¬¼ë¦½ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¡œì´í„° 2026-01-16 ë³´ë„ëŠ” ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„± í™•ëŒ€ êµ­ë©´ì—ì„œ ì‹œì¥ ë³€ë™ì„±ì´ í™•ëŒ€ë  ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì „í•˜ë©°, ì§€ì •í•™ì´ â€˜ë°©í–¥ì„±â€™ë³´ë‹¤ëŠ” â€˜ë³€ë™ì„±â€™ì— ë” í° ì˜í–¥ì„ ì£¼ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„ìœ¼ë¡œ í•´ì„ë  ì—¬ì§€ê°€ ìˆìŒì„ ë’·ë°›ì¹¨í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[8].

3. ì œí•œì  ìƒìŠ¹ ìš”ì¸
    

í•˜ë½ ì‹œë‚˜ë¦¬ì˜¤ì—ì„œë„ â€œì œí•œì  ë°˜ë“±â€ì„ ë§Œë“¤ ìˆ˜ ìˆëŠ” ìš”ì¸ì€ ì¡´ì¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ì§€ì •í•™Â·í•´ìš´ ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ëŠ” ì‚¬ê±´ ë°œìƒ ì‹œì ì— ë¦¬ìŠ¤í¬ í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì„ ì¬í˜•ì„±í•  ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë©°, ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ê°€ê²©ì„ ì§€ì§€í•˜ëŠ” ë°©í–¥ìœ¼ë¡œ ì‘ë™í•  ì—¬ì§€ê°€ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-15)[7]. ë‹¤ë§Œ IEAê°€ 2026ë…„ ì´ˆ ê³µê¸‰ ìš°ìœ„ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì„ ê°•ì¡°í•˜ëŠ” í™˜ê²½ì—ì„œëŠ”, í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ í™•ëŒ€ë˜ë”ë¼ë„ ì§€ì†ì„±ì´ ì§§ì•„ì§ˆ ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ìˆì–´ ê²°ê³¼ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ìƒìŠ¹ ì••ë ¥ì€ ì œí•œì ì¸ ìš”ì¸ìœ¼ë¡œ í‰ê°€ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤(2026-01-21)[1].

ë˜í•œ ë‹¨ê¸° ê°€ê²© í˜•ì„± ê³¼ì •ì—ì„œëŠ” ì‹œì¥ ì°¸ì—¬ìë“¤ì˜ ìœ„í—˜ ì„ í˜¸ ë³€í™”ë‚˜ ê¸°ì¡´ ê¸°ëŒ€ì˜ ì¡°ì •ì´ ê°€ê²© íƒ„ë ¥ì„ í‚¤ìš¸ ìˆ˜ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. 2026-01-16 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œì²˜ëŸ¼ ë¶ˆí™•ì‹¤ì„±ì´ í™•ëŒ€ë  ë•Œ ë‹¨ê¸° ë³€ë™ì„±ì´ ì»¤ì§€ë©° ê°€ê²©ì´ ì¼ì‹œì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì§€ì§€ë˜ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„ì´ ë‚˜íƒ€ë‚  ìˆ˜ ìˆê³ , ì´ëŠ” â€œì¼ì‹œì  ë°˜ë“±â€ì˜ ê²½ë¡œê°€ ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[8]. ë‹¤ë§Œ 2026-01-13 ë¡œì´í„° ë³´ë„ì—ì„œì²˜ëŸ¼ ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ ìƒë‹¨ì„ ì œí•œí•˜ëŠ” ì¬ë£Œë¡œ ì‘ë™í•˜ëŠ” êµ­ë©´ì—ì„œëŠ”, ë°˜ë“±ì´ ì¶”ì„¸ì  ê°•ì„¸ë¡œ ì „í™˜ë˜ê¸°ë³´ë‹¤ëŠ” ì œí•œì  ë²”ìœ„ì—ì„œ ì†Œí™”ë  ê°€ëŠ¥ì„±ì´ ìˆìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤[6].

4. ì‹œì¥ í•´ì„ ë° ì‹œì‚¬ì 
    

ì¢…í•©í•˜ë©´, í–¥í›„ 1ì£¼ì¼ ë¸Œë ŒíŠ¸ìœ  ì‹œì¥ì€ ê³µê¸‰ ì—¬ìœ ì™€ ì¬ê³  ë¶€ë‹´ì´ë¼ëŠ” êµ¬ì¡°ì  í•˜ë°© ìš”ì¸ì´ ìš°ì„¸í•œ ê°€ìš´ë°, ì§€ì •í•™Â·ë¬¼ë¥˜ ë‰´ìŠ¤ì— ë”°ë¥¸ ë‹¨ê¸° ë³€ë™ì„±ì´ ë³‘ì¡´í•˜ëŠ” êµ¬ê°„ìœ¼ë¡œ í‰ê°€ë©ë‹ˆë‹¤[1][2]. AI ìœ ê°€ ì „ë§ ëª¨ë¸ì˜ ì˜ˆì¸¡ê°’ì„ ê¸°ì¤€ìœ¼ë¡œ í–¥í›„ 1ì£¼ì¼ ìœ ê°€ íë¦„ì„ ì„¤ëª…í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[IA1]. ê¸°ì¤€ 65.88ì—ì„œ ì „ë§ 63.49ë¡œì˜ ë³€í™”ëŠ”, ë‹¨ê¸°ì ìœ¼ë¡œëŠ” ì´ë²¤íŠ¸ì„± í”„ë¦¬ë¯¸ì—„ì´ ì¶•ì†Œë  ë•Œ í•˜ë°© ì¬í‰ê°€ê°€ ìš°ì„¸í•´ì§ˆ ìˆ˜ ìˆìŒì„ ì‹œì‚¬í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤[IA1].
